<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>205 crore</span> (US$30 million)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boiworldwide_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-boiworldwide-3">[3]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

<p><i><b>My Name Is Khan</b></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varrev_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-varrev-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aka_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-aka-5">[5]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bollywood_films_of_2010" title="List of Bollywood films of 2010">2010</a> Indian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_film" title="Drama film">drama film</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a> and produced by Hiroo Yash Johar and <a href="/wiki/Gauri_Khan" title="Gauri Khan">Gauri Khan</a> and stars <a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a> in lead roles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinema_India_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cinema_India-6">[6]</a></sup> The film was jointly produced by <a href="/wiki/Dharma_Productions" title="Dharma Productions">Dharma Productions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_Chillies_Entertainment" title="Red Chillies Entertainment">Red Chillies Entertainment</a> and was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Fox_Searchlight_Pictures" title="Fox Searchlight Pictures">FOX Star Entertainment</a>, which had bought the rights for the film for a sum of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>100 crore</span> (US$15 million), making it the most expensive Bollywood film of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-companies_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-companies-7">[7]</a></sup> It is also the highest buyover for any Indian film, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ghajini_(2008_film)" title="Ghajini (2008 film)"><i>Ghajini</i></a>'s record of <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>90 crore</span> (equivalent to <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>176 crore or US$26 million in 2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before its release, the film generated a great deal of publicity for itself due to three main reasons: first, the multiple political controversies surrounding the film and its lead actor; second, Khan's presence in the film (he was last seen in a leading actor role in December 2008, when <i><a href="/wiki/Rab_Ne_Bana_Di_Jodi" title="Rab Ne Bana Di Jodi">Rab Ne Bana Di Jodi</a></i> was released); and third, the reunion of the "<i>golden pair</i>" of Khan and Kajol, who last appeared together in the film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabhi_Khushi_Kabhie_Gham" title="Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham">Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham</a></i> in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K.26SRK_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-K.26SRK-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> debuted in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UAE" title="UAE">UAE</a>, on 10 February 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-debut-11">[11]</a></sup> It premiered globally in cinemas on 12 February 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It was also screened as part of the <a href="/wiki/60th_Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="60th Berlin International Film Festival">60th Berlin International Film Festival</a>'s official selection the same month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berlin_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-berlin-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon its release, the film broke many box office records. <i>My Name Is Khan</i> was the highest-grossing Bollywood film overseas at the time, which was then overtaken by <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-14">[14]</a></sup> Within four weeks, the film crossed the <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>70 crore</span> (US$10 million) mark in India and became the first film of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bollywood_films_of_2010" title="Bollywood films of 2010">2010</a> to do so. In the overseas markets, the film grossed <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>110.34 crore</span> (US$16 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-os_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-os-15">[15]</a></sup> <i>My Name Is Khan</i> earned a worldwide gross of 200 crores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The film was released in India on DVD on 28 April 2010. <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> in India, plus a DVD release worldwide followed on 10 August 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rizwan Khan (<a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a>) is a Muslim child who grew up with his brother Zakir and his mother Razia Khan (<a href="/wiki/Zarina_Wahab" title="Zarina Wahab">Zarina Wahab</a>) in a middle-class family in Mumbai. Rizwan is different from other children, however. He has certain gifts, particularly a special ability to repair mechanical objects. His difference leads to special tutoring from a reclusive scholar and extra attention from his mother, both of which lead to heightened jealousy from his brother Zakir, who eventually leaves his family for a life in the United States.</p>
<p>Despite this resentment, as an adult Zakir (<a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Shergill" title="Jimmy Shergill">Jimmy Shergill</a>) sponsors Rizwan to come and live with him in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> after the death of their mother. It is at this time that Zakir's wife, Haseena, a psychologist, diagnoses Rizwan with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asperger%27s_syndrome" title="Asperger's syndrome">Asperger's syndrome</a>. Despite his limitations, Rizwan begins to work for Zakir as a sales rep for Zakir's company, a skin care product line. In the process he meets a Hindu woman, Mandira (<a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a>) and her young son, Sameer from a previous marriage. Mandira owns a successful high-end salon and is drawn to Rizwan's vulnerable honesty. Despite Zakir's hostility to the match and that it is forbidden for a Muslim man to marry a woman from religions other than from other Abrahamic faiths, Khan and Mandira marry and settle down in the fictional town of Banville. They live next door to Mark and Sarah Garrick and their young son, Reese. Both Mandira and Sameer take Rizwan's last name as their own.</p>
<p>The Khans' perfect existence gets disrupted, however, after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on New York City. Mark, a journalist, is sent to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">cover the war in Afghanistan</a> and dies there, much to both Sarah and Reese's distress. At the same time, the Khan family begins to experience hostility in their community, as well as other Muslims too and Reese begins to turn against Sam as well. One afternoon, an argument between them turns into a racially motivated schoolyard fight between Sameer and a gang of older students. Reese, acting on behalf of Sameer, tries to stop the fight, but is held back and Sameer, who pushes the gang to their temper by swearing at them, is finally finished off when a gang member kicks a soccer ball at him. Sameer later dies from his injuries. The gang then silences Reese by threatening to beat him up if he tells the authorities about it. A shattered Mandira blames Rizwan for Sameer's death, stating that Sameer "died only because his name was Khan." She then tells Rizwan that she no longer wants to be with him. When he asks her what he has to do to be together with Mandira, she sarcastically tells him that he has to tell the people of the United States and the President that his name is Khan and that he is not a terrorist.</p>
<p>Rizwan takes Mandira's request seriously, and thus sets out on a journey that takes him from one US state to another, in order to first meet President and later the new President-elect. During this quest, he travels to Wilhemina, Georgia and befriends Mama Jenny and her son Joel. It is revealed that Mama Jenny's husband, Joel's father, who was a U.S Army soldier, also died in the war in Afghanistan. Later, in Los Angeles, he prays in a mosque and overhears violent rhetoric from Dr. Faisal Rahman. He reports this to the FBI but there is no response at that moment. Later, while waiting in a crowd to meet President George W. Bush and repeating again and again, "My name is Khan and I am not a terrorist," Rizwan is arrested and placed in a prison by police who misinterpret his statement thinking he said he was a terrorist.</p>
<p>While in the prison he is interrogated as a terrorist suspect and meets the psychiatrist Radha who believes he is innocent. He is later released after a media campaign by some Indian student reporters Raj, Komal and Bobby Ahuja who prove his innocence by unearthing his attempts to inform the FBI about Faisal Rahman. After his release, he returns to hurricane-hit Wilhemina to help Mama Jenny and her son. His efforts attract media attention and numerous Muslims come to help as well, including Zakir and Haseena.</p>
<p>At the same time, a remorseful Reese confesses to Mandira and reveals the identities of the gang who killed Sameer. Mandira then simply says that it is still not enough. She then informs Detective Garcia who has been assisting her on the case, and Detective Garcia arrests the gang. Mandira later gets a call from Sarah to forgive Rizwan, "I've lost my husband; don't lose him."</p>
<p>Mandira realises her error, she joins Rizwan in Georgia, and their love rekindles. However, at the moment she arrives, Rizwan is stabbed by one of Dr. Faisal Rahman's followers, who accuses him of being a traitor to Islam, and Rizwan is rushed to the hospital. With Mandira's help, Rizwan survives and meets President-elect Barack Obama who tells him, "Your name is Khan and you are not a terrorist". The film concludes with Rizwan and Mandira going back home.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>, writer, co-producer and director of <i>My Name Is Khan</i>, the film is about a multitude of perspectives of the various opinions, facts, and propaganda that comes with the global issue of discrimination and intolerance towards a race of people completely unassociated with the evils of terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In an August 2009 interview, Shahrukh Khan stated that <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is "not about terrorism, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/11_September_attacks" title="11 September attacks">9/11</a>. It's about a relationship between two people, between an individual and the State, and between an individual and the country. In short, there are the three important components: a love story, Islam, and a mild form of <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meet_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-meet-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:40%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I think it's an exceptionally relevant time, as the unity of our nation is of paramount importance, and I am very happy to witness such a movement in front of my eyes. We are all coming together to fight for a common cause – called humanity. Everyone knows that terrorism has no religion and it will never have a religion. As a filmmaker, I believe that I have a social responsibility and I promise to fulfill that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">– <i><a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>'s response to the increased unification between Hindus and Muslims in India, especially after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/26/11" title="26/11">26/11</a>. As said to Madhureeta Mukherjee.</i></cite></div>
<p>In an earlier July 2009 interview, Khan also noted that the film focuses on themes concerning "the relationship between the Western world and Islam and how that has changed over the past few years." He describes the film as about "the journey of one family and how it changes because of 9/11" and suggests "we touch upon that in a very unbiased and educated way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In another early interview, he also stated that, "it's not about a disabled man's fight against disability. It's a disabled man's fight against the disability that exists in the world—terrorism, hatred, fighting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/..." title="...">...</a> <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is also about Islam and the way the world looks at Islam but we are not taking any sides. We are only trying to say that there are only good people and bad people. There are no good Hindus, bad Hindus, good Christians, bad Christians. Either you are a good person or a bad person. Religion is not the criterion, humanity is."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMW_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMW-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a> said in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a>: "<i>MNIK</i> is an unusual Bollywood film, if at all, and doesn't have those quintessential pre-requisite elements that any Bollywood film has. It's telling a story with a strong message, professing humanity and goodness and putting it out on a big cinematic scale. So all put together it is definitely a different experience for mainstream India (...) All I can say is that <i>MNIK</i> is going to open windows and doors to many people who have stories to tell and are shy to put their story on the celluloid" When asked about comparisons between the film and the 2009 release <i><a href="/wiki/Kurbaan_(2009_film)" title="Kurbaan (2009 film)">Kurbaan</a></i>, noting that both have dealt with similar topics, he added: "I'd say that Kurbaan didn't have 'hope', whereas MNIK had 'hope'. <i>Kurbaan</i> was more darker, grittier and a grey look at a situation, whereas <i>MNIK</i> is a hopeful, far more positive and a lot more positivity in its finishing reels with a triumph to the human spirit. <i>Kurbaan</i> was very cinematic and interesting in its approach but it didn't offer a solution. Rather it just tells the problem. <i>MNIK</i> offers you that solution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casting_and_filming">Casting and filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Casting and filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Production of the film took place in India and the United States. Filming began in Los Angeles during December 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMW_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-BMW-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and one of the locations used was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA">UCLA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Johar next continued production in Mumbai during April 2009. During June 2009, production moved to San Francisco<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">Bay Area</a>, where they filmed a key scene at the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Discovery_Museum_of_San_Jose" title="Children's Discovery Museum of San Jose">Children's Discovery Museum of San Jose</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahrukh_Khan" title="Shahrukh Khan">Shahrukh Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a> were cast in the lead roles, reuniting them after many years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kajolsrk_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-kajolsrk-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The film faced a temporary setback in late December when actor <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Bashir" title="Aamir Bashir">Aamir Bashir</a> was denied a visa to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> He was eventually replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Shergill" title="Jimmy Shergill">Jimmy Shergill</a> as Khan's younger brother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bonding_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bonding-32">[32]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Shabana_Azmi" title="Shabana Azmi">Shabana Azmi</a> was originally cast as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahrukh_Khan" title="Shahrukh Khan">Shahrukh Khan</a>'s mother<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> she left the production after his shoulder injury delayed the filming schedule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMW_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-BMW-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> She was replaced in the role by <a href="/wiki/Zarina_Wahab" title="Zarina Wahab">Zarina Wahab</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tanay_Chheda" title="Tanay Chheda">Tanay Chheda</a> portrayed Shahrukh Khan's character as a child living in the <a href="/wiki/Borivali" title="Borivali">Borivali</a> section of Mumbai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-junior_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-junior-35">[35]</a></sup> Chheda was chosen because he resembles Khan and because he is recognizable to an international audience after portraying "middle Jamal" in <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magna_Publishing_2015_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Magna_Publishing_2015-36">[36]</a></sup> He had earlier worked with Khan in the remake of the 1970s film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don:_The_Chase_Begins_Again" title="Don: The Chase Begins Again">Don: The Chase Begins Again</a></i>. American actor <a href="/wiki/Christopher_B._Duncan" title="Christopher B. Duncan">Christopher B. Duncan</a> was chosen to portray President Barack Obama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glamsham_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-glamsham-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toiinterview_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-toiinterview-38">[38]</a></sup> Duncan is known for his interpretation of Obama on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno_(1992_TV_series)" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno (1992 TV series)">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johar had difficulties finding a mosque to film in. According to actor <a href="/wiki/Arif_Zakaria" title="Arif Zakaria">Arif Zakaria</a>, "I don't know if Karan tried to get permission in Mumbai. But we were to shoot in a mosque in Los Angeles and hard as Karan tried to convince the authorities that his film would not propagate anti-social values, he was denied permission [...] We finally shot the two-day scene with Shahrukh Khan on the set of a mosque constructed at <i>The Club</i> in <a href="/wiki/Andheri" title="Andheri">Andheri</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denied_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-denied-40">[40]</a></sup> Johar also shot for an important scene inside of the studio of CBS 5 . San Francisco's Film Commission Director Stephanie Coyote was responsible for giving permission to the crew to shoot in the film studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>While shooting for the film, Khan suffered from severe pain in the neck and headaches which were caused by the expressions and posture of Rizwan Khan. His character in the film who has Asperger's Syndrome, has a way of jutting his neck out at a particular angle and wears an expression which has his eyebrows raised in every scene. As he would shoot for hours, he'd get severe migraines. Director Karan Johar admitted that "Shahrukh's character Rizwan had to arch his eyebrows and focus his eyes on a certain place before every take. Halfway through the shooting of the film, Shah Rukh developed severe headaches as result of all the pressure it would put on his head so he had to see a neurosurgeon for that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>After filming in Los Angeles was completed, Johar stated that, "in all my 11 years as a filmmaker I've never felt the experience to be so different. The content of <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is diametrically opposite to whatever I've done in the past."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bonding_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-bonding-32">[32]</a></sup> He described working with both Shahrukh Khan and Kajol again as "magic. They build an inexplicable energy on screen." Johar also stated that he was "blown away by Shahrukh who had done monumental research on his autistic character in the film. I was zapped by how much he knew about the subject."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bonding_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-bonding-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johar also asked Khan to co-produce the film under his production company <a href="/wiki/Red_Chillies_Entertainment" title="Red Chillies Entertainment">Red Chillies Entertainment</a>, Talking about the initiative, the director said:"we were both passionate about the subject, we said why not co-produce the film? We've known each other so long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/..." title="...">...</a> that this new initiative is just an extension of our emotions. Besides, I can never make a film without Shah Rukh."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elder_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-elder-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> debuted in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UAE" title="UAE">UAE</a> on 10 February 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-debut-11">[11]</a></sup> It released globally in cinemas on 12 February 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-release-1">[1]</a></sup> <i>MNIK</i> had a two phase release. To begin with, it had a mainstream release in India coupled with a regular Diaspora release in UK, US, Gulf, Australia and various other countries. "After that in the months of April and May, we would be looking at a mainstream theatrical release in countries like Germany, Poland and other parts of North America," detailed Johar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phased_releases_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-phased_releases-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="467" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg/220px-SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg/330px-SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg/440px-SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SRK_Kajol_%26_Karan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Khan, Kajol and Johar while unveiling the first look of the film</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> was screened as part of <a href="/wiki/60th_Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="60th Berlin International Film Festival">60th Berlin International Film Festival</a>'s Official Selection in February 2010, out of competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berlin_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-berlin-13">[13]</a></sup> The website <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> auctioned the tickets for the film's screening at the Berlin Film Festival for a record price of £1.000 (<a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">INR</a>60.000) each. All the tickets were sold out in five seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sel_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-sel-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first look of <i>My Name Is Khan</i> unveiled at a grand function at Mumbai by Johar, Khan and Kajol and was then be beamed across 70 countries worldwide on the Star TV Network. Says Karan, "This is a first in the history of Bollywood – that the promos of a film will play across such a wide platform. And, this has mainly been made possible because of our synergy with Fox Star Studios...and also the first time a Bollywood company is tying up with a mainstream Hollywood studio. So, there are many firsts to this venture."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The trailer of the film was released at the premiere of the Hollywood film, <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar" title="Avatar">Avatar</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K.26SRK_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-K.26SRK-10">[10]</a></sup> <i>My Name Is Khan</i> marked the first instance of a film using the <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Roadblock_(disambiguation)" title="Roadblock (disambiguation)">Roadblock</a> advertising technique to market a film, in which the three-minute trailer was aired on all leading television channels simultaneously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:40%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I will add that <i>MNIK</i> is a very special topic about humanity in the garb of a Muslim character [...] The film is made on a large canvas and the subject material is adapted in terms of humanity in a very entertaining way [...] the message of love, the way it has been shot internationally and the way of releasing it, might have all the possibilities of an international release. It is going to be released in a way no Hindi film has been released internationally before"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trailer_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-trailer-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">– <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahrukh_Khan" title="Shahrukh Khan">Shahrukh Khan</a>'s response to questions siting the film as "international" with a "far reaching influence" that should be seen by all</i></cite></div>
<p>The makers of the film made various brand tie-ups to for the promotion of the film. <a href="/wiki/Dish_TV" title="Dish TV">Dish TV</a> entered into a strategic marketing alliance with Fox Star and spend approximately Rs4 crore in a month-long 360 degree integrated marketing campaign which ran across all India to co-promote the brand and the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> created an entire <i>MNIK footwear and apparel collection</i> to promote the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sify_2010_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sify_2010-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 February 2010, Khan and Kajol became the first Indian movie stars to ring the opening bell of the New York stock exchange <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a>. They were invited by Fox Searchlight Pictures to do so as part of their promotion for <i>My Name Is Khan.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Shahrukh Khan also appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Friday_Night_with_Jonathan_Ross" title="Friday Night with Jonathan Ross">Friday Night with Jonathan Ross</a></i> as part of its promotion in the UK, becoming only the second Indian after <a href="/wiki/Shilpa_Shetty" title="Shilpa Shetty">Shilpa Shetty</a> to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-release_revenues">Pre-release revenues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Pre-release revenues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 7 August 2009, Karan Johar signed a deal for <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">INR</a> 1 billion with <a href="/wiki/Fox_Searchlight_Pictures" title="Fox Searchlight Pictures">Fox Searchlight Pictures</a>, who will market and distribute it in India (FOXSTAR) and worldwide (Fox Searchlight).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-companies_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-companies-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxdeal_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxdeal-55">[55]</a></sup> It covers all rights except music, which has been secured by Sony Music.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Subhash K. Jha (film critic and author of <i>The Essential Guide to Bollywood</i>) gave <i>My Name Is Khan</i> a rave review arguing that Rizwan Khan "repairs almost anything, including irreparably damaged relationships. But this film about damaged lives needs no repairing. <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is a flawless work, as perfect in content, tone and treatment as any film can get [...] <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is no ordinary film. Long after the wary-of-physical-touch Rizwan has finally shaken hands with President Obama, long after the heat and dust of racial and communal hatred has settled down the core of humanism that the film secretes stays with you. Yes, we finally know what they mean by a feelgood film."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skjrev_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-skjrev-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nikhat_Kazmi" title="Nikhat Kazmi">Nikhat Kazmi</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i> also gave it five stars, describing <i>My Name Is Khan</i> as, "indubitably one of the most meaningful and moving films to be rolled out from the Bollywood mills in recent times."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toirev_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-toirev-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taran_Adarsh" title="Taran Adarsh">Taran Adarsh</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a> gave <i>My Name Is Khan</i> four and a half out of five stars and argues, "When a film stars two of the finest talents of the country, you expect nothing but the best. SRK, well, how does one describe his performance? To state that this is his best work so far would be cutting short the praise he truly deserves [...] Kajol is pure dynamite and casting her for this character was the most appropriate decision. No other actress could've matched SRK in histrionics the way Kajol has. In fact, SRK and Kajol complement each other wonderfully well and this film only proves it yet again. It's a powerhouse performance from this supremely talented actress."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bh_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-bh-58">[58]</a></sup> Sarita Tanwar of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Day" title="Mid-Day">Mid-Day</a></i> gave the film four and a half out of five stars and described it as "near-perfect", concluding that "The Karan-Shah Rukh-Kajol combo strikes once more."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rajeev_Masand" title="Rajeev Masand">Rajeev Masand</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN-IBN" title="CNN-IBN">CNN-IBN</a></i> gave <i>My Name Is Khan</i> three and a half out of five stars, arguing that "the film shamelessly tugs at your heartstrings and on more than one occasion wallops you to weep. Aided by solid camerawork, tight editing and a layered story, Johar crafts an engaging, stirring saga that is earnest and noble. With this message movie in the mainstream format, the director takes a step in the right direction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-IBN_Review_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-IBN_Review-60">[60]</a></sup> Sudhish Kamath from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> wrote, "My Name Is Khan is populist, yet layered with rich political subtext. It's all about types, yet every character feels real. It's about generalisations and yet it chooses to dwell on the specifics. It's all heart and spirit that you can't help but overlook the flaws and admire it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> critic Manish Gajjar, who gave the film four out of five stars, the film is "a fiction-based film refreshingly told with realism of racial profiling on American soil. It's a rare treat for Hindi commercial cinema and a crossover audience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Pratim D. Gupta from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Telegraph_(Kolkata)" title="The Telegraph (Kolkata)">The Telegraph</a></i> in a positive review concluded, "<i>My Name Is Khan</i> has conscience and courage and two heartfelt performances. It can try your patience a bit but it will not leave you untouched."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Namrata Joshi from <i><a href="/wiki/Outlook_(magazine)" title="Outlook (magazine)">Outlook</a></i>, giving the film 3.5 out of 4 stars, described it as "a gentle, affecting and heart-warming film that makes you smile through your tears. It looks at contentious issues but offers overwhelming hope and renewal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> lists an approval rating of 81%, with 18 positive and 4 negative reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> As of 21 February 2010, the film has a score of 50 out of a scale of 100 on the review aggregate website <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, based on 7 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rachel Saltz of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> states, "<i>Khan</i> is one of a handful of Hindi films (<i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(film)" title="New York (film)">New York</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Kurbaan_(2009_film)" title="Kurbaan (2009 film)">Kurbaan</a></i>) about Indians living in a paranoid, post-9/11 America, and there's something fascinating about looking at this country through a <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> lens, even when the story is a kind of fairy tale. (Most interesting here is the link made between black Americans and Indians, especially Muslims.) Skilfully directed by Karan Johar and with an evocative score by Shankar, Ehsaan &amp; Loy, <i>Khan</i> jerks tears with ease, while teaching lessons about Islam and tolerance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytrev_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytrev-67">[67]</a></sup> According to Kirk Honeycutt of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollywood_Reporter" title="Hollywood Reporter">Hollywood Reporter</a></i>, <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is, "a film that delves compellingly into Americans' anti-Muslim hysteria" as it tackles "a subject American movies have mostly avoided – that of racial profiling and the plight of Muslim-Americans. It also allows Shah Rukh Khan to display his talent to an even wider audience. It's well worth the 162-minute journey."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrrev_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-hrrev-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jay Wesissberg of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> describes <i>My Name Is Khan</i> as a "riotously overstuffed and enormously enjoyable drama" with "confident camerawork [which] is matched by exceptional production design" He also states that Shah Rukh Khan and Kajol are a "delight together and her natural warmth makes the relationship even more believable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varrev_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-varrev-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> was not India's official entry to the Oscars as best foreign language film, but it made it to the reminder list of films eligible for the 83rd <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> opened very well in most places across the world, and set many records in the process.However, the performance of the film could not sustain beyond the first or second week in some places, including India and USA. The film's performance in India was quite good but still is generally regarded as "below expectations" due to the high price, while the overseas performance of the film has been record breaking. As of 4 April, the worldwide gross revenue for <i>My Name Is Khan</i> from the box office is US$36,145,870. Domestically, <i>My Name Is Khan</i> generated INR 727 million net (equating to INR 967 million gross).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India_2">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In India, the film opened with a massive INR 295 million (US$6,356,688), which was the third-highest weekend net for a Bollywood film, behind <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ghajini_(2008_film)" title="Ghajini (2008 film)">Ghajini</a></i>. It recorded the third-highest first day business across India, behind <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ghajini_(2008_film)" title="Ghajini (2008 film)">Ghajini</a></i> at the time of release. The film broke the record of <i><a href="/wiki/Race_(2008_film)" title="Race (2008 film)">Race</a></i> for the biggest opening weekend in the first quarter of the year. The film was reported to have done very well in multiplexes, but comparatively on the lower side in single screens. The film managed to net INR460.8 million (US$9,952,857) in its first week</p>
<p>In rankings based on distributor share, My Name Is Khan comes in fifth behind <i><a href="/wiki/Dabangg" title="Dabangg">Dabangg</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajneeti" title="Rajneeti">Rajneeti</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Golmaal_3" title="Golmaal 3">Golmaal 3</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Housefull_(2010_film)" title="Housefull (2010 film)">HouseFull</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> in a way bearing out Sajid Khan's boast that <i>HouseFull</i> will surpass MNIK in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The film managed to retain the No. 1 spot at the Indian box office for two consecutive weeks, and remained in the top five for six consecutive weeks. At the end of its theatrical run, the film earned ₹82.51 <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">crore</a> (US$12,698,289) in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas">Overseas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Overseas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> grossed US$23 <a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">million</a> in the overseas markets making it the highest grossing Bollywood film overseas at the time<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> and now 5th <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Indian_films_in_overseas_markets" title="List of highest-grossing Indian films in overseas markets">Highest grossing Indian film in overseas markets ever</a>. The film grossed the biggest opening day overseas, taking an estimated <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">INR</a>170 million, beating the overseas opening day collections of <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i>. The film also grossed the biggest opening weekend overseas, taking an estimated INR 255 million, again beating the overseas opening weekend collections of <i>3 Idiots</i> which grossed INR 185 million. In its first week, it grossed INR393 million (US$8.5 million). As of August 2010, the film has grossed $4,018,771 in the United States and $37,001,087 elsewhere for a worldwide total of $41,019,858.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo1_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo1-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the UK, it made £123,000 on its opening day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> which was more than the combined total of <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> in its first two days (£121,000). By the end of the second week, MNIK became only the third Bollywood film to cross the £2 million mark in the UK, after <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Veer-Zaara" title="Veer-Zaara">Veer-Zaara</a></i>, according to the exchange rates prevailing at their respective times of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> debuted in USA in 120 theatres, breaking the record set by <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> which debuted in 119 theatres. The film broke the record for an opening weekend in the US, earning US$1,994,027. The film debuted at No. 13 at the American box office. By the end of the first week, the film grossed US$2,552,283, second only to <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i> which had a Christmas holiday week. By the fourth week, the film earned US$3,868,891 (INR193,820,016), breaking Shahrukh Khan's previous record set by <i><a href="/wiki/Om_Shanti_Om" title="Om Shanti Om">Om Shanti Om</a></i>. On the 51st day of screening in the US, <i>My Name Is Khan</i> broke the US$4 million barrier, and became only the second Bollywood film ever to cross this mark, after <i>3 Idiots</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo1_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo1-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, the film earned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A$" title="A$">A$</a>39,000 (INR16.1 lakhs) on its opening day, and was ranked No. 11 in the market. By the first weekend, the film earned US$437,687, defeating the previous record set by 3 Idiots (US$350,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ausg_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-ausg-80">[80]</a></sup> In New Zealand and Fiji, the film earned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NZ$" title="NZ$">NZ$</a>13,627 on its opening day, and earned NZ$144,831 (US$100,698) in its first week. By the end of its theatrical run, the film earned NZ$232,586.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> the response to the film has been described as "huge" and it earned approximately US$300,000 on its opening day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-84">[84]</a></sup> In Egypt it earned one million <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_pound" title="Egyptian pound">Egyptian pounds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> By the end of its theatrical run, the film grossed US$517,018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> also opened well in Sri Lanka, Pakistan and the Far East. The film is the highest-grossing film in Pakistan, breaking the records set by <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i>, <i>3 Idiots</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wanted_(2009_film)" title="Wanted (2009 film)">Wanted</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frwm_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-frwm-87">[87]</a></sup> By its third week, MNIK has become the highest-grossing Bollywood film in the Middle East, earning US$3.3 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehindu_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-thehindu-88">[88]</a></sup> In South Africa, the film earned US$85,214 (Rs. 39.28 lakhs) in its opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sabo_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-sabo-89">[89]</a></sup> In Malaysia, it earned <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_ringgit" title="Malaysian ringgit">MYR</a>105,527 (US$31,106) in its opening weekend, and by the second weekend, the film had earned MYR410,864 (US$120,452).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sabo_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-sabo-89">[89]</a></sup> In Nigeria, the film earned an "impressive" <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_naira" title="Nigerian naira">NGN</a>2,310,137 (US$15,362) in its opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sabo_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-sabo-89">[89]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, the film earned <a href="/wiki/Ghanaian_cedi" title="Ghanaian cedi">GHS</a>10,599 (US$7,443) by the second weekend. In Indonesia, the film has grown from six to 14 screens and has seen a jump of 300 percent in week three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehindu_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-thehindu-88">[88]</a></sup> The film has also grossed $425,825 in 7 weeks at the Bahrain box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The film has also grossed an impressive $55,073 in Poland in its opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The film grossed $270,698 in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The film also made $58,683 in Lebanon region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <i>My name is Khan</i> released in Hong Kong on 5 January 2012 and collected $107,197.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_records">Box office records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Box office records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>My Name Is Khan</i> created several records, both in India and around the world. In India, the film smashed the record for a Bollywood release in the month of February, breaking the previous two-year record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Jodhaa_Akbar" title="Jodhaa Akbar">Jodhaa Akbar</a></i>. The film also broke the record for a Bollywood release in the first quarter of the year, breaking the previous two-year record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Race_(2008_film)" title="Race (2008 film)">Race</a></i>. In the UK, the film broke the four-year record of <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna</a></i>, and became the highest-grossing Bollywood film in the UK. In the Middle East it is also the highest grossing Bollywood film. As of date <i>My Name Is Khan</i> is the second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Bollywood_highest-grossing_films_in_overseas_markets" title="List of Bollywood highest-grossing films in overseas markets">highest-grossing film in overseas markets</a>, next to <a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a> which was released in newer markets in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in December 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overseas_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-overseas-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_analysis">Performance analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Performance analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film faced considerable falls in collections after its first week. The drops in collections is evident from the fact that 63% of the film's net collections came from the first week, as compared to 54% for <i><a href="/wiki/Race_(2008_film)" title="Race (2008 film)">Race</a></i>, 56% for <i><a href="/wiki/Ghajini_(2008_film)" title="Ghajini (2008 film)">Ghajini</a></i>, 49% for <i><a href="/wiki/Rab_Ne_Bana_Di_Jodi" title="Rab Ne Bana Di Jodi">Rab Ne Bana Di Jodi</a></i> and 39% for <i><a href="/wiki/3_Idiots" title="3 Idiots">3 Idiots</a></i>. In spite of this, the film managed to retain the No. 1 position at the box office for two consecutive weeks. It was in the top 5 list of the Indian box office for six consecutive weeks. Though the mid-week collections saw a drop of 60% from the opening weekend, it held up well against other major releases and secured the highest first quarter collections, a record previously held by the 2008 film <i>Race</i>. Thus, the film is a financial success owing to its record-breaking overseas collections and healthy domestic collections.</p>

1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span> <a class="external text" href="http://movies.rediff.com/report/2010/jan/07/my-name-is-khan-music-review.htm" rel="nofollow">link</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The soundtrack is composed by the critically acclaimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shankar-Ehsaan-Loy" title="Shankar-Ehsaan-Loy">Shankar-Ehsaan-Loy</a>, who previously teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a> to give hit music for his movies like <i><a href="/wiki/Kal_Ho_Naa_Ho" title="Kal Ho Naa Ho">Kal Ho Naa Ho (2003)</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna (2006)</a></i>. The lyrics are penned by <a href="/wiki/Niranjan_Iyengar" title="Niranjan Iyengar">Niranjan Iyengar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myikmusic_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-myikmusic-101">[101]</a></sup> The music was released on 5 January 2010, by Sony Music Entertainment (India) who has also previously released the music for <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar's</a> movies <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Khushi_Kabhie_Gham..." title="Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...">Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...(2001)</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna</a></i>, which gained global musical success. The musical soundtrack consists of 6 original songs and 4 bonus tracks that are taken from <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>'s previous successful films that have featured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahrukh_Khan" title="Shahrukh Khan">Shahrukh Khan</a>. The soundtrack includes one <a href="/wiki/Instrumental" title="Instrumental">instrumental</a> called "Khan Theme", composed by Indrajit Sharma and the strings for the song are performed by the Bombay Film Orchestra. The songs such as "Noor-e-Khuda" blend western bar blues and techno sounds with Indian classical styles such as <a href="/wiki/Sufi_music" title="Sufi music">Sufi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">Hindustani</a>. The song "Allah hi Rahem" sung by Ustad <a href="/wiki/Rashid_Khan_(musician)" title="Rashid Khan (musician)">Rashid Khan</a> is another example of Sufi thematic song. The soundtrack is thus representative of the "indie fusion genre". Unlike <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>'s other films, this film has no lip-sync songs. All the songs are in background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srkjaved_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-srkjaved-102">[102]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception_2">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Upon its release, the album received generally positive reviews from most music critics. Gianysh Toolsee of <i>Planet Bollywood</i> states that the soundtrack is "very much about transcending the boundaries set by Bollywood by venturing into an emotional state through Sufism and spirituality."Joginder Tuteja of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a> gives the album a three out of five stars, suggests that director Karan Johar along with musicians Shankar-Ehsaan-Loy and lyricist <a href="/wiki/Niranjan_Iyengar" title="Niranjan Iyengar">Niranjan Iyengar</a> "have brought not a partial but a substantial difference to the way music in [Johar's] films is being looked at."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyrics">Lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Niranjan_Iyengar" title="Niranjan Iyengar">Niranjan Iyengar</a> is alone credited for writing the lyrics for the songs, Niranjan penned the only two Sufi songs in the film, "Sajda" and "Allah Hi Rahem". The famous lyricist, <a href="/wiki/Javed_Akhtar" title="Javed Akhtar">Javed Akhtar</a> was approached to write the lyrics for the remaining three songs. Earlier it was reported that he refused to write lyrics, because Javed Akhtar did not want to share the credits with another lyricist since Niranjan Iyengar has written two songs for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radiosargam.com_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-radiosargam.com-104">[104]</a></sup> Later <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a> confirmed that Javed Akhtar penned the remaining songs, but Javed did not want him to be credited as the lyricist when the soundtrack released as he had to share the credits with Nirinjan Iyenger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srkjaved_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-srkjaved-102">[102]</a></sup> Javed confirmed this and said, "I don't like to share the credits. I would have got the publicity but the other person, who has done a fine job, wouldn't have. I have read the songs penned by Niranjan and I think he has done a great job."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srkjaved_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-srkjaved-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radiosargam.com_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-radiosargam.com-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_security">Airport security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Airport security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Khan has stated that due to his last name and religion, he (like Rizwan Khan) is frequently subject to excess security checks at airports. On 14 August 2009, Khan arrived in the United States to promote <i>My Name Is Khan</i> and to participate in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Asian" title="South Asian">South Asian</a>-related events around the country (including <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(India)" title="Independence Day (India)">Indian Independence Day</a>). Upon arriving at <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, he was pulled aside by immigration officers after his name popped up on their computers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> questioned for over an hour (Khan claims it was at least two hours) about the nature of his visit, and was later released. According to the <i>Times Online</i>, "In Delhi, Timothy J. Roemer, the American Ambassador to India, said that the embassy was trying to 'ascertain the facts of the case.' He added: 'Shah Rukh Khan, the actor and global icon, is a welcome guest in the United States.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi_frontpage_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-toi_frontpage-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Khan said he was told that it was because "they said my name was common to some name that popped up on the computer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-held_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-held-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-more_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-more-109">[109]</a></sup> The officials asked if he could provide names of people to vouch for him. Khan noted that he "had all the documents; they were asking me where I was going to be staying. I gave the name of FOX people with whom I had finalised a deal a few days ago as contacts." However, because they wanted to check his luggage which the airline had lost, Khan said that he "was taken to a room where many people were awaiting a secondary check on visa, most were South Asians. In fact many officers were reluctantly vouching for me, some people were asking for autographs and a <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistani</a> fan even said he knew who I was. But the officers said it was procedure and kept taking numbers from me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-held_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-held-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:40%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I did feel bad for a lot of people in that room, I know because I had an escort and someone would recognise me, I will get out. Others may face more trouble [...] I have extra security because of my name. I can handle this but when you have someone as respectable as an ex-president getting frisked, I am nobody (in reference to the frisking of President <a href="/wiki/A._P._J._Abdul_Kalam" title="A. P. J. Abdul Kalam">A. P. J. Abdul Kalam</a> earlier in the summer).[...] I think it is a procedure that needs to be followed. But it is an unfortunate procedure."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><i><a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a> on being frisked at <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Airport</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-held_108-2"><a href="#cite_note-held-108">[108]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>While he was not allowed to use his own phone, Khan was permitted one phone call.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi_frontpage_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-toi_frontpage-106">[106]</a></sup> He was thus released after officials from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embassy_of_India_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of India in Washington, D.C.">Indian Consulate</a> intervened. Civil Aviation Minister Praful Patel stated that the event will be further explored with U.S. officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-more_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-more-109">[109]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, "Elmer Camacho, a spokesman for the US Bureau of Customs and Border Protection, said the questioning was part of the agency's routine process to screen foreign travellers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> When asked if he would demand an apology, Khan replied that he would not.</p>
<p>The director of <i>My Name Is Khan</i>, <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>, was asked during an August 2009 interview with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiD_DAY" title="MiD DAY">MiD DAY</a></i> if the event was a publicity stunt for the film. Johar denied that it was and responded: "It's upsetting because I got a text message this morning asking me if it was publicity plug for my movie. (Sarcastically) I mean, if I had that much power over the Homeland Security, why would I allow Shah Rukh to go through something like this? [...] What's really shocking is the fact that when I was writing the film, I never thought that what happened to the protagonist of the film would happen to Shah Rukh."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> During a January 2010 interview, Khan referred to the implication that the event was a publicity stunt for the film as "lowdown and cheap."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hopes_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-hopes-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_B._Duncan" title="Christopher B. Duncan">Christopher B. Duncan</a>, who portrays <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama</a> in <i>My Name Is Khan,</i> also commented on the incident stating: "I was very disappointed with what SRK experienced at the airport. We're living in times where the levels of fear can sometimes spill over into paranoia. Here's a man who is an international superstar, being detained for an excessive amount of time at an airport in the United States. It had to be very upsetting for him. Imagine <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah (Winfrey)</a> being detained at an airport in India for a long time, during a kind of interrogation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toiinterview_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-toiinterview-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, the incident sparked debate and commentary among Indian politicians, actors, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> It also led to demonstrations in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> California Governor <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> later invited Khan to have dinner with him "in a bid to diffuse what has become a slight diplomatic row."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>In another event, on 5 February 2010, while promoting <i>My Name Is Khan</i> on the British talk show <i><a href="/wiki/Friday_Night_with_Jonathan_Ross" title="Friday Night with Jonathan Ross">Friday Night with Jonathan Ross</a></i>, Khan claimed that female security staff at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> in London had printed a naked image of him taken using the newly installed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_scan" title="Security scan">body scanner</a> that he was asked to go through. He said that he autographed it for them, though it is not clear if his comments were intended as a joke. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAA_Limited" title="BAA Limited">BAA</a> spokeswoman for Heathrow Airport has denied his claim. She claimed that it was "completely factually incorrect", stressing that images captured using the equipment could not be stored or distributed in any form and that his claims "simply could not be true."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>In relation to Khan's comments, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economic_Times" title="The Economic Times">The Economic Times</a></i> has raised concerns over the new body scanners and the possibilities of it being abused to distribute naked pictures of celebrities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> His comments have restarted the debate in Britain over whether the new scanners violate individual privacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shiv_Sena_controversy">Shiv Sena controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Shiv Sena controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Shahrukh Khan (who owns the <a href="/wiki/Kolkata_Knight_Riders" title="Kolkata Knight Riders">Kolkata Knight Riders</a> cricket team) criticised the fact that members of the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_Pakistan" title="Cricket in Pakistan">Pakistani Cricket Team</a> were not bought by the clubs competing in the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a> (IPL), he was condemned by <a href="/wiki/Shiv_Sena" title="Shiv Sena">Shiv Sena</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu_nationalist" title="Hindu nationalist">Hindu nationalist</a> political party. There were consequent protests and demonstrations against him and demands that cinemas in India refuse to screen <i>My Name Is Khan</i>. Khan responded by stating, "What did I say that was wrong? All I said was that I wanted people to come to my country."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cricket_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-cricket-123">[123]</a></sup> Khan continued by stating that: "I have no idea what I am supposed to apologise for [...] If I am in wrong I would like to apologise but someone needs to explain to me what is wrong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-no_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-no-124">[124]</a></sup> He also stated that he does "not want any confrontation. I am trying to explain myself on every platform [...] I have not said anything that is anti-national." Khan said that he was willing to meet with <a href="/wiki/Bal_Thackeray" title="Bal Thackeray">Bal Thackeray</a> to discuss the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noapol_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-noapol-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, Shiv Sena rescinded its demand to block release of <i>My Name Is Khan</i> after it was announced that Khan would be allowed to release it "in as many theatres" as he would like.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glad_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-glad-126">[126]</a></sup> However, on 10 January 2010, when cinemas opened for advanced bookings, individuals disguised as "cinegoers" began to attack cinemas and booking centres. Director Karan Johar and distributors met with police to ask for additional security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uturn_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-uturn-127">[127]</a></sup> In response, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Maharashtra" title="Chief Minister of Maharashtra">Chief Minister of Maharashtra</a> <a href="/wiki/Ashok_Chavan" title="Ashok Chavan">Ashok Chavan</a> threatened to withdraw security cover for party leader Uddhav Thackeray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-withdraw_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-withdraw-128">[128]</a></sup> Later, some security was withdrawn and the <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> government has "called in five battalions of the State Reserve Police Force to protect 63 cinemas in the city that will screen the film directed by Karan Johar from this Friday." There were multiple arrests and leave of all police officials were cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-over_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-over-129">[129]</a></sup> The distributor, Fox Star, stated that the film would still be released on its scheduled opening date, 12 February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dist_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-dist-130">[130]</a></sup> It opened to full cinema houses across India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=My_Name_Is_Khan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</ul>
